        <p class="date">
         Thu Jul 31, 2014 at 12:56 AM PDT
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2014/07/31/1317695/-GOP-impeachment-fleecing-scam-backfires-they-ve-lost-the-narrative-maybe-a-midterm-advantage" id="titleHref">
          GOP impeachment fleecing scam backfires - they've lost the narrative &amp; maybe a midterm advantage
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/Eric Nelson">
          Eric Nelson
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=231987&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/07/31/1317695/-GOP-impeachment-fleecing-scam-backfires-they-ve-lost-the-narrative-maybe-a-midterm-advantage" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="GOP impeachment fleecing scam backfires - they've lost the narrative &amp; maybe a midterm advantage" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/07/31/1317695/-GOP-impeachment-fleecing-scam-backfires-they-ve-lost-the-narrative-maybe-a-midterm-advantage" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="98" data-story_id="1317695" href="/story/2014/07/31/1317695/-GOP-impeachment-fleecing-scam-backfires-they-ve-lost-the-narrative-maybe-a-midterm-advantage#comments">
           98 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <p>
          <a href="http://talkingpointsmemo.com/dc/the-huge-republican-advantage-2014-midterm-elections">
           Sahil Kapur @ Talking Points Memo
          </a>
          has listed the mathematical (and other) republican advantages in this upcoming 6th year midterms (February 20, 2014)
          <br/>
          ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Even
          </strong>
          if the RWNJ's in house had the numbers to indict/impeach, there isn't the 2/3rds needed in the senate to
          <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment">
           convict
          </a>
          . But the 'elite' GOP leadership does seem to have lost control where it takes them, so who knows how far the RWNJ's will go with this
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Just for the record
          </strong>
          The GOP survive on scams like this years long impeachment con job. Without scandals, con jobs, fear mongering, hate peddling, division, threats, and all the many other low down tricks; they don't win. They can't. The republican party has nothing that informed people want or need and would vote for. The republican party does not represent people, at least not the vast majority of people. Not even a little bit.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           So
          </strong>
          when Boehner and to many other republicans claim they want the "threat" of impeachment to end - they are
          <strong>
           lying and fundraising
          </strong>
          off their ill represented constituents while they're at it.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://www.msnbc.com/now-with-alex-wagner/watch/impeachment-threats-a-boon-for-dems-313380931748#">
           <big>
            Alex Wagner @ NOW and her team put together a video montage
           </big>
          </a>
          of republicans as far back as 2010 starting with Darrell Issa debunking every word from house speaker John Boehner who is now
          <strike>
           claiming
          </strike>
          spinning that he and republican leadership are against this impeachment "threat"
          <br/>
          <small>
           (btw the video has a short ad - sorry | and that I am unable to embed the new MSNBC video player/platform -
           <em>
            it's worth a look see
           </em>
           )
          </small>
          <br/>
          <br/>
          <strong>
           <big>
            The Boehner spin:
           </big>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <big>
           "..it's all a scam started by, uh, Democrats at the White House"
          </big>
          <p>
           - John Boehner | July 29, 2014
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          <strong>
           The good news is that republican old guard may not have it together enough to limit this latest impeachment fundraising/GOTV drive to mere threats or a
           <a href="http://www.politicususa.com/2014/06/26/white-house-rips-john-boehners-taxpayer-funded-lawsuit-president-obama.html">
            ridiculous tax payer funded lawsuit
           </a>
           this time around. If the house does impeach, the republicans may suffer unexpected losses and Dems, a better than usual midterm - good - republicans pay dearly for their destructive shenanigans and
           <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nullification_(U.S._Constitution)">
            "nullify"
           </a>
           themselves
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           <big>
            This
           </big>
          </strong>
          from
          <a href="http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/21-million-reasons-why-dems-love-the-gops-anti-obama-push">
           Steve Benen
          </a>
          lays out how the GOP burned their own backsides 16 years ago..
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          In 1998, congressional Republicans, filled with irrational rage towards a Democratic president in his sixth year, launched an impeachment crusade the American mainstream saw as wildly unnecessary. The electoral results were striking: Bill Clintons Democratic Party had the best sixth-year midterms of any administration in a century.
         </blockquote>
         ..and are heading down the same destructive path into another 6th year midterm election that would help Dems electoral prospects - again
         <p>
          <strong>
           <big>
            This
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandering_(politics)">
             political pandering
            </a>
            has been going on for years now:
           </big>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          
          <strong>
           Darrel Issa
          </strong>
          (2010) republican congressman - Ca.:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "This is serious, this is an impeachable offense according to Dick
          <small>
           <a href="http://www.salon.com/2014/04/17/dick_morris_is_very_afraid_a_horrible_pundits_popular_vote_hysteria/">
            [hilariously wrong]
           </a>
          </small>
          Morris. The allegation is one that everyone from Arlen Specter to Dick Morris have said is in fact a crime and could be impeachable"
         </blockquote>
         
         <strong>
          Steve Stockman
         </strong>
         republican congressman - Texas:
         <blockquote>
          "We want all tools available to use including that, the impeachment"
         </blockquote>
         
         <strong>
          James Inhofe
         </strong>
         republican senator - Oklahoma - @ a radio interview:
         <blockquote>
          <strong>
           Inhofe:
          </strong>
          "To me, we may be starting to use the I-word before too long"
          <p>
           <strong>
            Host:
           </strong>
           "Okay, the I-word meaning impeachment?"
          </p>
          <p>
           <strong>
            Inhofe:
           </strong>
           "yeah"
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         
         <strong>
          Michelle Bachmann
         </strong>
         republican congresswoman, past and possible
         <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/07/23/michele-bachmann-2016_n_5613029.html">
          2016
         </a>
         republican presidential candidate - Minnesota:
         <blockquote>
          "There isn't a weekend that hasn't gone by that someone says to me - 'what in the world are you all waiting for in congress? 'why aren't you impeaching the President?' "
         </blockquote>
         This is the same
         <em>
          passing the blame to an unverifiable source
         </em>
         kind of story Bachmann told when another unknown "someone" convinced her that mental retardation is indisputably caused by flu vaccines, or the fairy tale no one believed at the time, that republicans have no intention of shutting down the government,
         <u>
          which they did
         </u>
         ; or that no one in their right mind would hold hostage the full faith and credit of the US by threatening to default on raising the debt limit, thrilled at the prospect of using
         <a href="http://thehill.com/homenews/house/330283-house-gop-says-sequester-is-leverage-in-next-budget-battle">
          sequestration for political leverage
         </a>
         <em>
          (rather than allowing for a sensible budget)
         </em>
         ,
         <u>
          which they also did
         </u>
         , costing for the first time in history, a
         <a href="http://blogs.wsj.com/marketbeat/2011/08/05/sp-downgrades-u-s-debt-rating-press-release/">
          downgrading of our triple A rating
         </a>
         with one of the premiere credit rating agencies.
         <p>
          <strong>
           <big>
            With more impeachment pandering from republicans
           </big>
          </strong>
          <em>
           who have not then nor have ever
           <strike>
            been a member of..
           </strike>
           talked about Bircher/birther/impeachment
          </em>
          - yeah right, not a word except for all the time for the last 5 years - that is
         </p>
         <p>
           Minority Whip
          <strong>
           Jon Kyl
          </strong>
          (R-Ariz.), the #2 Republican in the chamber at the time, telling a broadcast:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "Now if its bad enough and if shenanigans involved in it, then of course
          <a href="http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/impeachment-not-toy-redux?lite">
           impeachment is always a possibility
          </a>
          . But I dont think at this point anybody is talking about that.
         </blockquote>
         lol - a "possibility" that "nobody is talking about" - except that you just did Kyl
         <p>
          
          <strong>
           Todd Akin
          </strong>
          (R-Mo.) said in April 2013 he wanted to impeach Obama because of:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          all of the czars
         </blockquote>
         
         <big>
          Meanwhile
         </big>
         ,
         <strong>
          Rep. Cliff Stearns
         </strong>
         (R-Fla.) talked in March 2013 about impeaching Obama -
         <a href="http://maddowblog.msnbc.msn.com/_news/2012/03/13/10666675-florida-congressman-joins-birther-brigade">
          cuz freedomz
         </a>
         <p>
          
          <a href="http://mediamatters.org/video/2012/01/06/cavuto-can-obama-be-impeached-for-recess-appoin/185904">
           Fox News Neil Cavuto
          </a>
          speaks with republican rep. Bill Johnson (Ohio) suggesting in 2012 that Obama might be liable to impeachment over recess appointments
          <small>
           (video @ link)
          </small>
          :
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "that sounds like an impeachable offense"
         </blockquote>
         
         <a href="http://thinkprogress.org/politics/2011/03/02/147590/franks-impeach-doma/">
          Rep. Trent Franks
         </a>
         (R-Ariz.) raised the prospect of impeaching Obama over DOMA:
         <blockquote>
          I would support that in a moment, remarked Franks  he went on to say that he would absolutely favor impeaching President Obama and Attorney General Eric Holder if such a move could gain collective support
         </blockquote>
         
         <a href="http://blogs.star-telegram.com/politex/2011/08/burgess-puts-impeachment-on-the-table.html">
          Rep. Michael Burgess
         </a>
         (R-Texas) talked up the idea of presidential impeachment because:
         <blockquote>
          "It would tie tings up" [in Washington for a while, making governing impossible.]
         </blockquote>
         
         <strong>
          Rep. Walter Jones
         </strong>
         (R-N.C.) even introduced an
         <a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2012/03/a-resolution-to-impeach-is-ready-if-obama-goes-to-war-without-congress/254366/">
          impeachment resolution
         </a>
         , just in case Obama sends U.S. troops to Syria.
         <p>
           Then there is the republican rising "personhood" star
          <a href="http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/the-republican-partys-i-team">
           Joni Ertz
          </a>
          :
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "
          <a href="http://news.yahoo.com/joni-ernst---impeachment--of-obama-should-be-on-the-table-204439051.html">
           Impeachment
          </a>
          of Obama should be on the table"
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          
          <strong>
           <big>
            <big>
             Even
            </big>
           </big>
          </strong>
          the old boat anchor republican
          <strong>
           John McCain (R - Arizona)
          </strong>
          passed around the impeachment feculence:
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "We're not going to impeach the President because we don't have sixty seven votes in the United States senate in order to do so. But I do think that a lawsuit filing about the Presidents abuse of his power - which he has clearly done some fifty five times, or whatever it is on Obamacare alone - then I think that's probably a good idea'
         </blockquote>
         So McCain instead of rejecting the whole impeachment crap because it's stupid and has a well documented racist underpinning at its core, chooses a half-assed
         <em>
          cya
         </em>
         by bringing up the lack of votes as the reason not to impeach.
         <p>
          But he never rejected the idea outright, and doesn't stop there. He actually pretends to buy into the "let's sue the President" of the United States of America hogwash. This from establishment "tort reform' the "frivolous lawsuit" hating GOP.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           McCain and other old guard GOP buying into the lawsuit thing?
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <big>
           Wow.
          </big>
         </p>
         <p>
          Years and years have been spent by the right honing that mocked up "burdensome regulations" - "frivolous lawsuit" - we need "tort reform" - meme in order to sever/eliminate consumer protections and instead protect unscrupulous corporate business practices that hurt real people
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           That right there
          </strong>
          tells me that the GOP "old guard' is and has been using this impeachment obsession for
          <strong>
           "purely political reasons"
          </strong>
          -&gt;
          <em>
           <small>
            (the latest GOP accusation meme currently under development - iow's in the testing stages to see if the shit sticks)
           </small>
          </em>
          knowing full well it's another
          <a href="http://www.cpa-connecticut.com/blog/?p=2242">
           con-job
           <small>
            (video with Cenk Uygur)
           </small>
          </a>
          they can't let happen yet can't let go, not because the RWNJ fringe
          <u>
           <strong>
            won't
           </strong>
          </u>
          really try for impeachment, but because they
          <u>
           <strong>
            will
           </strong>
          </u>
          , while the money pours in along with a fired up base of voters exactly as it has been doing for the GOP
         </p>
         <p>
          Beholden to a tiny minority of corpo "interests" they shill for, the establishment GOP can't politically afford to stop this impeachment nonsense, as powned representatives of a
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/07/21/1315597/--Stealing-Not-a-plank-but-the-very-foundation-of-the-GOP-platform">
           party based on theft
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          All because of who the GOP choose to represent; or rather who they aren't allowed to represent - real people that is - leaving the GOP with an agenda no well informed working person would knowingly go for
          <br/>
          ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
         </p>
         <p>
          The GOP at this low point in their history have made their choice of representation plain. They have long ago
          <u>
           chosen
          </u>
          this kind of idiocy as if it's all they have to gin up their demographically shrinking base. Maybe it is considering what they represent..but..
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           But they don't need it.
          </strong>
          If they had decent policies that favored the middle class, a huge majority, they could actually compete without enacting Jim Crow laws. But they and their agenda are bought and paid for by a tiny minority of wealthy Oligarchs. An agenda that if they were forced, like the movie
          <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liar_Liar">
           "Liar Liar"
          </a>
          with Jim Carrey, to tell the whole truth of it, no one would ever vote for who wasn't already filthy rich and into protecting a life of living off of the labor of others
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           What is a bit surprising though
          </strong>
          is that the republicans including Boehner think that they are fooling anyone one into believing that they don't want this birther variant, this impeachment "threat" coming from the fringe. This political and moral squalor. Refusing to let go of the myth of "trickle down"-voo-doo-fairy-dust-capital-trumps-labor-platform, the GOP are now mired in their own a pile of stink because of the choices they themselves have made. The choice to support a hierarchal system that favors the already affluent 1%ers while oppressing the majority of the people using chaos, disinformation, with divide and conquer methods to keep the "unwashed masses" fighting each other; limiting the average persons time, social mobility, and the financial wherewithal to focus on the real culprit - the tiny minority paying for the GOP to exist
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           <big>
            The good news is
           </big>
          </strong>
          , it sure seems to me, is the people. The republican party is losing the ability to keep people in the dark as they used to so completely - word is spreading amongst the people
         </p>
         <p>
          Sometimes a party has to hit rock bottom before they can recover. Or better yet for the country the GOP, just dies. Not that the fight is be any means over but the GOP seem well on their way down and justly so.
         </p>
         <p>
          In a two party system both party's are supposed to represent a plurality of the two largest constituencies made up of real people of all ages, races, and creed, or numbers close to that. Based on the actual platform of the GOP catering to a tiny minority, that hasn't been true of the GOP for a long time.
          <br/>
          Let the 1%ers, the John Galt's finally take that walk they always threaten when taxes are mentioned - and good riddance - but not before we take back through taxation and other methods of recouping what is long owed and was siphoned off the top of our labor first - that is
         </p>
         <p>
          So this post is "just for the record" post. "Nothing of social or political import" -
          <small>
           (Janis Joplin paraphrased - I think)
          </small>
          ..or offering solutions. Just taking note, voicing my opinion and trying to help push back on the lies and look at some truth for a change
         </p>
         <p>
          With a blast from the past with Rachel Maddow called:
         </p>
         <p>
          "Time for the RIght to leave the Bubble"
          <br/>
          <small>
           (short ad - sorry)
          </small>
          <embed allowfullscreen="true" allowscriptaccess="always" flashvars="launch=49736294^775170^965098&amp;width=640&amp;height=360" height="360" name="msnbc38cd5b" pluginspage="http://www.adobe.com/shockwave/download/download.cgi?P1_Prod_Version=ShockwaveFlash" src="http://www.nbcnews.com/id/32545640" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="640" wmode="transparent">
          </embed>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           - thank you
          </strong>
          for stopping by :)
         </p>
         <p>
          It's gotten late now so I'll be back tomorrow
         </p>
         <p>
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          P.S. Sorry JeffW but Sarah Who had this to say. I couldn't pass this up.
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "I absolutely and passionately believe it is possible.
          <p>
           And first I believe liberals want us to believe that they love hearing this talk of impeachment because they are going to be able to turn it around for their re-election bids.
           <br/>
           It's kind of a reverse psychology thing that they're playing on us and some people are buying into it.
           <br/>
           And that's why I'm going to ne even more adamant about explaining why we should impeach"
          </p>
          <p>
           - source Up with Chris Hayes July 29, 2014 via Michael Medved show - Monday
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          - lol
         </p>
         <p>
          GOP, Hoist on their own petard, burnt by their own hateful excretions and
          <strike>
           they wonder why
          </strike>
          they're angry this latest con job is failing and support for Dems is on the rise
         </p>

           <span class="cu">
            The plural of parties is parties. Not party's. ...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1317695/54087837#c11?mode=alone;showrate=1#c11">
             5+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">

            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:985170">

             <a href="/user/uid:116838">
              elwior
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            The plural of parties is parties.  Not party's.  An apostrophe does not denote a plural, ferchrissakes.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:580318">
             Sally Foster
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1317695/54087837#c11">
             Thu Jul 31, 2014 at 05:31:04 AM PDT
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <ul class="cm i1" id="k54087837">
         <li id="c14">
          <div class="cx" id="cx54087890">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Being pedantic
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1317695/54087890#c14?mode=alone;showrate=1#c14">
              6+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:22584">
               highacidity
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:76686">
               middleagedhousewife
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:116838">
               elwior
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:333891">
               Smoh
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:92045">
               ColoTim
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:3312">
               Odysseus
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             You can use the apostrophe for plurals of symbols (A's, 3's, ...) and acronyms/initialisms and similar constructions (IRA's, 401k's). This used to be mandatory, but as far as I can tell is now optional, unless not using the apostrophe results in confusion.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
            </p>

          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:2138">
              Yosef 52
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:1003349">
              silverfoxcruiser
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I don't know if it would help Republicans in 2014-2016, but their impeaching Clinton in 1998 helped them then. There was no change in their 1999 Senate majority, and only a small (steady) loss in their retained House majority. They undermined the Clinton legacy that should have elected Gore easily, including alienating Gore from Clinton to the extent of putting Clinton backbiter Lieberman on the Gore ticket. Which put Gore's ballot victory close enough to steal in 2000 for Bush/Cheney, while they retained each chamber of Congress.
           </p>
           <p>
            It was all very close, and they did lose a few seats along the way to make it close. But it worked. Without the Lewinsky scandal, they had nothing to run on, especially given the Clinton economy and the extraordinarily peaceful international scene. With it, crystallized and forced into daily (hourly) news reports by actual impeachment, they seized control of the US and drove us down their nightmare road. That we're still on, despite getting a (nominally, perhaps) driver.
           </p>
           <p>
            So while I'm not at all sure their impeachment PR campaign, or even actual impeachment, would help them now, I'm pretty sure that Republicans would think it would. Their defining characteristic is living not just in the past, but in the past as seen on TV. They'd love nothing more than a rerun of 1998-2001.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

            <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/user/DocGonzo/diary" rel="nofollow">
             turn pro
            </a>
            ." - HST
           </p>

            Another Republican ploy fails. Sucks to be them...
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1317695/54097465#c89?mode=alone;showrate=1#c89">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:323657">
              twocrows1023
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:1027531">
              Bluegeorgia
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            If the Republicans' impeachment talk has caused them to lose the narrative, and perhaps even a midterm election advantage, then they have only themselves to blame. Suddenly trying to put the onus for the constant diatribes concerning the "Impeach Obama" movement, promulgated by right-wing politicians and talking heads on the cable news networks (Fox News) and conservative radio talk shows, on the Obama administration and the Democrats is not only an exercise in futility, it's laughable. The Republicans have routinely insulted the American electorate's intelligence with their shameful attempts to deflect the blame for the I-word issue onto the liberals.
           </p>
           <p>
            The disgusting impeachment narrative has failed to gain steam with voters, and it's actually helped the Democrats in soliciting campaign contributions and emphasizing how important it is for liberal voters to cast their ballots in November. Now that the Republicans' nefarious impeachment ploy has backfired, many of them, including House Speaker John "Tan Man" Boehner, have been dissembling, obfuscating and discombobulating the public discourse on this issue, quickly attempting to change the subject before it does any further damage to their party's candidates' chances of winning the election.
           </p>
           <p>
            The conservatives have greatly miscalculated their premise that most Americans hate Obama just as much as they do, when in fact We The People are SICK TO DEATH of even MORE Republican obstructionism in Congress. In their attempts to thwart the White House's and the Democrats' forward progress, and to destroy President Obama's legacy, they've brought the business of our federal government to a screeching halt. Will the voters blame the Republicans for throwing around the red herring of impeachment to take attention away from the REAL issues facing America today? Do they finally realize that the Republicans hate Obama more than they love our country? Hopefully so. (fingers crossed) Sucks to be them...
            <br/>
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:317463">
             Tigger Too
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1317695/54097465#c89">
             Fri Aug 01, 2014 at 06:58:03 AM PDT
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <ul class="cm i1" id="k54097465">
         <li id="c92">
          <div class="cx" id="cx54100019">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Yep.  Sucks to be them.
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1317695/54100019#c92?mode=alone;showrate=1#c92">
              2+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:15497">
               Bjorkee
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:1027531">
               Bluegeorgia
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <blockquote>
             The conservatives have greatly miscalculated their premise that most Americans hate Obama just as much as they do,
            </blockquote>
            They just keep sitting in their ivory tower and ignoring the facts:
            <br/>
            FACT: There was a poll in 2008, remember it?
            <br/>
            Obama more than doubled the take of McCain in the electoral college, with 365 electoral votes to McCain's 173; he received the largest percentage of the popular vote for a Democrat in nearly a half-century.
            <p>
             FACT: There was another in 2012.
             <br/>
             And Obama had a vote total well in excess of 62 million, as compared with Mitt Romneys 58.8 million.
            </p>
            <p>
             Obama has just kept winning the polls that matter and Bitter-Old-Man McCain et al just can't get past it.
            </p>
            <p>
             On the linked clip of Alex Wagner's NOW, McCain said that the reason why the house wouldn't impeach Obama was because the Senate didn't have the votes to convict. Not because it was frivolous [which it is] but because the Senate couldn't deliver.
            </p>
            <p>
             That's neither here nor there, however. Cruz wants it and, even though he's not a member of it, we all know the House will give him anything he wants. Yeah, because that government shut-down worked out so well for them.
            </p>
            <p>
             The shut-down likely won't affect this year's election. It was too long ago and the American people's memory is too short for it to have an impact.
            </p>
            <p>
             The current lawsuit, however, and all the talk of impeachment are happening less than 3 months before the election and will just continue getting more shrill between now and then. The Tea Party diehards want Obama impeached but no one else does. So what does this mean? Democrats [the most unlikely folks to turn out during an off-year election] are almost certain-sure to show up in droves this November. All this talk of the Reps keeping the House and taking the Senate could be stood on its head.
            </p>
            <p>
             McCain SHOULD know it [that's why I'm so certain that it's his bitterness talking. By his calculation, HE should be the guy in the WH.]
            </p>
            <p>
             Boehner knows how dangerous the whole business is but is powerless to stop it. Cruz is undercutting him.
             <br/>
             And Boehner is SUING the president for acting unilaterally while, at the same time saying, "Why doesn't Obama act on his own on this border thingy?"
             <br/>
             Seriously, this is what passes for leadership in this country these days.
            </p>
            <p>
             Palin is too clueless to understand that she could very well be handing both houses of Congress to the Dems. The same is true of Bachmann. And Cruz.
             <br/>
             Hey, you guys. Just keep on doing what you do. You're going to hand the nation back to a modicum of sanity despite your best efforts.
            </p>
            <p>
             And Hallelujah!
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
             The price of apathy is to be ruled by evil men - - Plato . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . We must be the change we wish to see in the world - - Mohandas Gandhi
            </p>

          <li id="c96">
           <div class="cx" id="cx54102472">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              You're preaching to the choir there, brother!
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1317695/54102472#c96?mode=alone;showrate=1#c96">
               0+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              You've pretty much addressed the problem for the Democrats if they're counting on those Republican nimrods beating the dead horses of impeachment, suing President Obama, and their 50+ attempts to repeal and replace (with WHAT is anybody's guess) the Affordable Care Act as their sole strategy for winning in November. As we learned from the government shutdown last October, some American voters are IQ-challenged, having notoriously short memories and the attention spans of fleas. Progressive candidates must be proactive in their efforts, instead of merely being reactive to whatever bullshit non-issues the conservatives can dredge up next and use as shiny objects to wave in front of the electorate's faces to distract them. Those Republicans might be dumber than a box of rocks, but they're also sneaky-snakes.
             </p>
             <p>
              Thanks to the Republicans rigging elections in their favor via Citizens United, district gerrymandering, suppressing voters' rights and other such skulduggery, they've gifted themselves with a distinct advantage over the Democrats in the upcoming election. These lazy, lying, thieving, Obama-hating bums have shown that they're willing to win elections by hook or by crook, and anybody with the sense God gave a goose knows it.
             </p>
             <p>
              If (God forbid!) the Republicans DO maintain a majority in the House and DO end up taking the Senate as well, then the past six years of Obama's presidency are going to look like a goddamn picnic in comparison. I mean, can you only IMAGINE the amount of damage they could do to America over the next two years if they held both houses of Congress? They'd have Obama, the Democrats and We The People by the short-hairs in an even tighter grip, for sure. My pubes are smarting over the mere thought of such a disastrous outcome in November. Yikes.
             </p>

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });

		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });

		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
